## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population size P, which is the core problem in population ecology. Classical models range from exponential growth to density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, no density dependence)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible curvature)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal forcing on logistic growth)
- Harvesting/immigration logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (logistic with constant immigration or harvesting)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial approximation of growth rate)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (rational density dependence with mortality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ P) indicates density-independent exponential growth as the base mechanism
- Quadratic term in P (P² term) indicates pairwise intra-specific competition or cooperation (logistic-type density dependence)
- Cubic term in P (P³ term) often indicates Allee effects where both low and high densities reduce per-capita growth
- Logarithmic dependence on P (log(P)) suggests Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically
- Rational functions of P (P/(1+P)) indicate saturating competitive interactions or resource limitation following Michaelis-Menten-like kinetics
- Periodic functions of t (sin/cos of t) indicate seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing on growth parameters
- Exponential functions of t indicate non-stationary environments with systematically changing conditions
- Product of multiple factors involving P (e.g., P*(P-a)*(K-P)) indicates multiple population equilibria and bistability
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where c≠1,2) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling or allometric metabolic constraints
- Absence of explicit t dependence suggests an autonomous system where growth depends only on current state (most classical ecology models)

$$0.7124 \cdot P - 0.7124/68.906 \cdot P^2 + 0.7124 \cdot P^{1/3} + 0.7124 \cdot P \cdot \exp(-0.03459 \cdot t)$$
